**The pattern (marketing positioning split from objective measurement, routed via alias to the objective canonical) is roast-level-specific today** — none of the other 9 axes have a clean marketing-positioning dimension that overlays the canonical. But the pattern generalizes: any future case where a noisy positioning vocabulary obscures a clean measured / objective canonical is a candidate for the same split.

**Inventory measurement workflow** (Chris-articulated 2026-05-16, not in `roast-levels.md` today) — Chris's process for converting purchased-roasted bags into measured-path objective-bucket data: (1) at buy time, mark the peak-rest date on the bag (typically 4-6 weeks post-roast for Moonwake-style washed coffees, varies by roaster + cultivar + process per the `roaster.restCurve` field); (2) at peak rest, open the bag, run the Lighttells CM200 to capture whole-bean Agtron; (3) record the reading in Chris's **inventory sheet inside claude.ai** (distinct from the Latent app's `green_beans` inventory, which is self-roasted-only); (4) portion the remaining beans into 15g doses in scientific vials, vacuum-seal, freeze. The inventory sheet is what claude.ai cross-references at recipe-design time when working with stored coffee. The workflow started recently — many older coffees in Chris's freezer pre-date it and have no measured Agtron, which is what creates the inferred-path dependency.
_Avoid_: "roaster tag" (close but loses the *marketing-positioning* framing), "roast style tag" (close — but roast style is the persistent property; marketing tag is the language used to express it), "positioning tag" (under-specified), "bag word" (informal — useful in prose), "ultralight" / "Nordic Light" without the umbrella (specific instances, not the umbrella term).

**Auto-created provenance**:
The audit-trail enum recording **whether a canonical FK row was matched against an existing entry at write time (`canonical`) or freshly materialized by the write itself (`auto_created`)**. Today's storage: `green_beans.terroir_provenance` + `green_beans.cultivar_provenance` + `brews.terroir_provenance` + `brews.cultivar_provenance` (Phase 3, migration 045), paired with `green_beans.canonicals_updated_at` timestamp that bumps when the FK changes via patch or future canonical re-resolution. The provenance flag is set by the find-or-create write path: alias-lookup → canonical-check → if no canonical row exists, materialize one with full metadata from the registry entry AND set `*_provenance = auto_created`; if the canonical row was already present, set `*_provenance = canonical`. Either way the write succeeds — provenance never blocks the write; it just records what happened so the arbiter procedure can review later.

**Provenance + override-flag are dual mechanisms for the same concept** — both record whether a canonical-axis input matched an existing canonical vs. lazily materialized, but use different storage shapes:
- **FK-creating axes (cultivar, terroir)**: provenance enum column on the entity (`canonical` | `auto_created`), because these axes have FK rows that exist independently of any brew / green_bean
- **Text-only override-eligible axes (producer, roaster, brewer, filter, grinder, + future signature_method)**: `*_override: true` boolean parameter at write time + queue entry in `taxonomy_overrides_queue`, because these axes have no FK row — the canonical is the string itself

The two mechanisms achieve the same outcome (the write succeeds + the canonical-promotion decision lands in arbiter scope) but reflect the underlying axis storage shape. **Strict axes (cultivar / terroir today) have one more state**: if the find-or-create can't even resolve canonically-or-aliasably, the entity write fails fast and claude.ai's recovery path is `propose_canonical_addition` — a separate Tool that queues the canonical decision without the entity write succeeding. The strict-fast-fail behavior is what distinguishes FK-creating-strict (cultivar / terroir) from FK-creating-with-override-fallback (which no axis uses today but the architecture would support).

**The provenance flag is the operational mechanism for the Pick-not-author principle's exception path**: when pick succeeds, write proceeds with `canonical` provenance + full registry-metadata materialization; when pick fails, the write doesn't block at the claude.ai layer — it falls back to materialize-with-flag + queue for asynchronous arbitration. This is what lets claude.ai's authoring workflow remain unblocked even on imperfect canonical coverage.

**Per-axis NET-NEW behavior expected** (Chris-articulated 2026-05-16):
- **Cultivar / Terroir**: auto-create + arbitrate (FK-materialize lazily; arbiter promotes / aliases / rejects)
- **Producer**: auto-create + arbitrate; high NET-NEW rate expected (the "most inclusions" axis)
- **Roaster**: auto-create + arbitrate; pretty good coverage but never complete
- **Flavor**: try-harder-before-creating ("flavor is very subjective, should figure that out if it really truly cannot fit"); when truly net-new, auto-create + arbitrate
- **Roast level**: closed-loop, no creation possible (8 buckets exhaust the Agtron scale)
- **Brewer / Filter**: rarely fires for Chris's writes because the owned set is comprehensive; override-flag handles unowned encounters
- **Grinder**: never fires (self-only, Chris owns what he owns)
- **Process** (base + subprocess + modifiers): try to decompose first; if can't, auto-create + arbitrate
- **Signature method**: try to fit existing canonicals; if claude.ai thinks something is truly proprietary, auto-create + arbitrate + promote to signature canonical

**Origin story (Belle era)** — provenance + the canonical taxonomy systematization both trace to the EA-handoff moment when Chris's spreadsheet workflow scaled beyond him. Chris held all the resolution logic in his head; his EA Belle, working with her own AI assistance, didn't have the coffee domain context and produced (a) **generative variability** — the same coffee filled differently across runs because "AI models are generative by nature, don't always produce the same results" — and (b) **alias-resolution gaps** ("is Panamanian Geisha the same as Geisha?"). The systematization response made the EA's job pick-the-canonical + let-other-fields-materialize, with provenance recording when picking failed so the failure became visible (arbitration queue) rather than silent (downstream drift).
_Avoid_: "creation provenance" (close — but the enum specifically distinguishes pre-existed vs lazy-materialized, not creation-in-general), "row provenance" (under-specified — could mean any creation audit), "auto-creation flag" (close — but "flag" is overloaded against `*_override:true` flag), bare "provenance" (overloaded — the field is specifically about canonical-axis materialization timing).

**Skeleton entry**:
A canonical entry promoted with **minimal authored content** + an explicit `skeleton: true` flag indicating that rich-field research is pending — the resolution to "promote now with the data we have OR wait until research is done" when a NET-NEW canonical earns promotion but the data at promotion-time is incomplete. The flag exists on rich-registry shapes (today only `ProducerEntry`, but the pattern would extend to roaster / brewer / filter when needed). Today's only instance: **Miguel Estela** (authored from existing brew row geography — Peru / Cajamarca / Northern Andean Highlands / Maracaturra — pending the 27-field producer research).

**The flag makes under-researched promotion visible rather than silent** — a skeleton entry looks deliberately different from a richly-authored one (page render can surface "needs research" indicators; arbiter sees the flag during queue sweeps; future readers know the thin content is a known incomplete state, not assumed-done). The flag is **monotonic-then-deleted** — flip to false (and remove the flag entirely) when the rich content is backfilled; never deleted without the content being filled, because the canonical still has to exist for downstream brews to reference.

**Skeleton entries should surface in the arbiter procedure as a third queue surface** (Chris-locked 2026-05-16) — today the procedure walks `doc_proposals` + `taxonomy_overrides_queue`; adding skeleton review extends the same trigger phrase ("process pending arbitration") to a third queue. The arbiter's job per skeleton entry: (a) confirm the canonical really belongs as a separate entity (vs. should-be-aliased / should-be-rejected as drift retroactively); (b) if yes, fill in the remaining rich-field content — collaboratively between Chris (domain knowledge) and Claude Code (research + drafting). This closes the **self-improvement loop on the canonical layer** — skeleton entries flow through arbitration into full rich entries, the registry gets richer per arbitration run, and the Pick-not-author principle's runtime experience gets thicker (claude.ai's pick at runtime returns more registry metadata, less authoring required).
_Avoid_: "stub entry" (close — but stub is overloaded with code-test-stub meaning), "partial entry" (under-specified — many entries are partial in some sense; skeleton is specifically the flagged-incomplete shape), "draft entry" (close — but draft implies not-yet-canonical; a skeleton entry IS canonical, just thin), "placeholder" (under-specified — could mean many things), bare "minimal" (under-specified).

**Family palette**:
The deliberate-hue-separated color-coded parent-level grouping applied across **five canonical-registry axes** today — roaster (6 strategy families), cultivar (8 genetic families: 5 Arabica + 3 non-Arabica), flavor (8 families: Citrus / Stone Fruit / Berry / Tropical / Grape & Wine / Floral / Tea & Herbal / Sweet & Confection + Other), process base (4 hues for Washed / Honey / Natural / Wet-hulled), country (12 country hues for terroir). Each axis's palette lives in a dedicated `lib/*-colors.ts` or as part of the registry mirror's `getFamilyColor` exports; each follows the design-conventions rule **hue-not-lightness** — if a signal deserves its own color, shift hue, not lightness.

**Distinct from Parent level**: Parent level is **hierarchical-taxonomy-specific structural ancestry** (species/family/lineage for cultivar; country/admin/macro for terroir); Family palette is the **render + semantic color scheme** keyed to a parent-level grouping. They overlap on cultivar (genetic family is both a parent level AND a family-palette unit) and terroir country (a parent level AND a family-palette unit), but family palette extends to non-hierarchical axes too: roaster strategy families and flavor families have no underlying parent-child structural taxonomy, just the family-coded color grouping. **Distinct from Aggregation level**: family palette is always *above* the aggregation level (groups for visual hierarchy on index pages, never the canonical unit itself).

**Three functions of family palette**:
1. **Visual grouping on aggregation index pages** — `/roasters` groups by family with family-colored section headers; `/cultivars` groups by species → family → lineage with family-coded swatches; `/processes` groups by base color.
2. **Color-coded chips / tags on detail pages** — strategy pills, flavor-note family coloring, terroir country swatch on `/terroirs/[id]`.
3. **Synthesis-prompt anchor context** — per-entity synthesis adapters (terroir / cultivar / process / roaster) reference the family color or the family name as anchor metadata in the directed prompt.

**Origin** — the family palette emerged because the precursor claude.ai-local app rendered every brewing recipe card the same color, which became monotonous and hard to scan as the archive grew. The first color schema was **flavor-note-based** — floral → pinkish tone, fruity → brighter, tea-like → greenish, chocolatey → browner / darker. Once that was working, the same monotony problem recurred on terroir / roaster / cultivar / process indexes, and the pattern extended axis-by-axis with each axis's families getting a deliberate hue mapped to its semantic content. **Color carries semantic encoding** (Chris's framing): clarity-first → light + delicate hues; extraction push → red (aggressive); suppression → slate. The palette is *informational*, not decorative — at-a-glance index browsing surfaces "this is stronger" / "this is more tea-like" / "this is heavier" without reading the text. **The framing comes from coffee being organic material** with flavor + aromatics + sensation; the visual encoding has to carry more dimensionality than a typical app to keep scanability when the corpus grows.
_Avoid_: "color scheme" (under-specified — too generic; family palette is specifically the canonical-axis-keyed grouping), "axis palette" (close — but the per-axis framing is part of family palette's definition, not an alternative noun), "family colors" (informal — works in prose, but `Family palette` is the canonical noun for the umbrella pattern), "render palette" (close but loses the *semantic-encoding* framing), "category palette" (close but category is overloaded — flavor BASE has categories distinct from families).

**Strategy tag**:
The **roaster-axis-specific leaf-positioning label** that names how a roaster characteristically directs their roasting + brewing intent — more granular than family palette, mechanically collapses to family via `STRATEGY_TAG_FAMILY` in `lib/roaster-registry.ts`. 10 strategy tags today + SELF-ROASTED, mapping to 6 families: `CLARITY-FIRST` → Clarity-First; `BALANCED` → Balanced; `BALANCED → CLARITY` → Balanced (slight clarity skew on cooling); `BALANCED → FULL` → Extraction-Forward; `BALANCED → HIGH` → Extraction-Forward (synonymous with FULL EXPRESSION); `FULL EXPRESSION` → Extraction-Forward; `SYSTEM` → System; `VARIES` → Varies; `BALANCED / VARIES` → Varies (Strait, Switch); `SELF-ROASTED` → Self-Roasted.

The **`→` arrow syntax** in tags like `BALANCED → FULL` names a *skew direction* — the roaster's home position is BALANCED but they push toward FULL when the coffee + process calls for it. Distinct from `FULL EXPRESSION` (no skew — Full Expression is the home position). The arrow encodes positional nuance without forking a new family.

**Cross-axis vocabulary coherence rule** (Chris-locked 2026-05-16) — strategy tag vocabulary on roaster must align with extraction strategy canonical names on brews. "My Clarity-First when I brew things should match the Clarity-First on a roaster's house style — we can't have too much drift between those." Today's alignment is **partial**: roaster `CLARITY-FIRST` ↔ brew `Clarity-First` align; roaster `FULL EXPRESSION` ↔ brew `Full Expression` align; but brew `Suppression` / `Extraction Push` / `Hybrid` have no direct roaster-tag equivalent (no roaster positions as Suppression-specific; `BALANCED → HIGH` is the closest tag to Extraction Push; no `Hybrid` roaster tag because Hybrid is a structural strategy distinct from extraction-intensity positioning), and roaster `SYSTEM` / `VARIES` / `SELF-ROASTED` are roaster-only constructs with no brew equivalent (a brew always names a specific strategy, even on a SYSTEM or VARIES roaster's coffee). The coherence rule is **aspirational** today and earns a vocabulary-audit follow-up.

**Strategy tag is the input to the Roaster signal at Coffee Brief Step 1c** — claude.ai reads the roaster's strategy tag (via the `roaster.strategyTag` field on the canonical entry, propagated through the synthesis-prompt anchor) as one of the three signals (variety / process / roaster) feeding strategy-direction arbitration. **Roaster strategy = starting point, not destination** (Chris's framing): roaster house style + published brew guide give claude.ai a strong typical-brewing inference, factored into the Coffee Brief but not copied — Chris's own brewing reality may diverge through iteration. Same shape as the roasting-side "expectations vs. reality" delta — sometimes the brewed cup matches the roaster's intent, sometimes it doesn't, and the divergence is signal worth recording.

**Origin — the Motta story** — pre-Motta, Chris's strategy palette didn't include `FULL EXPRESSION` as a roaster tag. The Jeferson Motta anaerobic-washed Gesha wrong-zone trap (Moonwake-roasted, originally iterated as Clarity-First, eventually unlocked by Full Expression — already canonical in CONTEXT.md as the brewing-iteration-loop-within-strategy example) forced the strategy tag to be added retroactively. Same iterative authoring pattern as the rest of the canonical-registries cluster — strategy tags emerged bottoms-up from real brewing experience, not designed top-down. Moonwake itself carries `VARIES` rather than a fixed-direction tag — they don't roast for one characteristic, the strategy is process + coffee dependent, and that fact itself is the load-bearing signal.
_Avoid_: "house style" (close — house style is the broader concept that strategy tag is one input to; see existing Roaster signal / House style entry), "positioning label" (under-specified — many things are positioning), "strategy direction" (close — but direction is part of the tag content via the `→` syntax, not the whole tag), bare "tag" (overloaded), "roaster strategy" (informal — fine in prose; "Strategy tag" is the canonical noun for the registry field).

### WBC Reference Materials

**WBC reference materials**:
The cluster of four research-derived docs — [docs/brewing/wbc-reference.md](../../docs/brewing/wbc-reference.md) / [docs/brewing/wbc-recipes.md](../../docs/brewing/wbc-recipes.md) / [docs/roasting/wbc-roasting.md](../../docs/roasting/wbc-roasting.md) / [docs/roasting/wbc-sourcing.md](../../docs/roasting/wbc-sourcing.md) — that project the World Brewers Cup competitor corpus onto Latent's worldview. Sit in a distinct architectural layer above individual brew / lot records but below the master refs ([BREWING.md](../../BREWING.md) / [ROASTING.md](../../ROASTING.md)): read by claude.ai at workflow time via MCP `read_doc`, **advisory rather than enforcing**, never a validation target. Distinct from canonical taxonomies (which validate writes), the glossary (CONTEXT.md, which defines vocabulary), the personal archive (`docs/roasting/archive.md`, per-lot compounding doc), and the operational prompts (workflow-step-mapped instructions).

**Origin — three threads converging late 2026-04 / early 2026-05**:
1. **The post-Motta question** "are there entire strategy zones I don't even know about?" — extending the existing strategy-geography metaphor (strategy = country, sub-form / modifier = state, iteration = city) one level *up*: "what continents am I missing?" The Motta wrong-zone trap (pre-Two-Axis-Framework) had only been escapable retroactively; the WBC research was the *proactive* mapping that prevents future Mottas.
2. **The canonical-registries bottoms-up authoring methodology** being applied in parallel to cultivar / terroir / process / producer taxonomies — the same iterative-convergent collect → draft → test-against-data → iterate pattern, transferred to WBC corpus collection. The WBC research is one more instance of the same authoring discipline.
3. **The V2 MCP build sprint** making research a productive way to spend Claude-Code-wait-time.

**Authoring source** — YouTube transcripts of WBC routine presentations. Every competitor talks through their recipe + style + water + intent during the live routine; transcripts back-populated a spreadsheet that became the corpus. **Two-pass construction**:
- **First pass (2026-05-03, Sprint 2.7)** — 1st / 2nd / 3rd winners 2022-2025, ~18 recipes. Drove the canonical strategy enum's first WBC-triggered expansion: pre-WBC was `Clarity-First` / `Balanced Intensity` / `Full Expression`; first pass added `Suppression` + `Extraction Push`, reaching 5 intensity strategies + the Two-Axis Framework.
- **Second pass (2026-05-06, v8.4)** — all participants (not just top 3) 2022-2025, 102 recipes. World Brewers Cup competitors are themselves the national-best winners of their countries' Brewers Cup competitions, so even round-one participants carry meaningful signal. The second pass produced the 5 foundational control axes + 8 strategy families + ~38 subtypes, and drove the Hybrid promotion to a 6th first-class strategy.

Recipe-level signal is bottoms-up decomposed into 5 axes + 8 families + ~38 subtypes — the same methodology used for cultivar / terroir / process / producer canonical taxonomies, applied to a different domain.

**Data-density asymmetry across the 4 docs** — brewing is the most complete because that's what competitor routines are primarily about; sourcing-side and roasting-side data are **byproducts** of the brewing data collection (competitors mention their coffee + producer + roast in passing, but in less detail than they talk about the brewing recipe). The asymmetry is preserved in the doc structure: `wbc-reference.md` + `wbc-recipes.md` carry the full bottoms-up decomposition; `wbc-roasting.md` is an open-ideas hypotheses doc (~100 entries, mostly 2-5 lines each, no equivalent 38-subtype taxonomy); `wbc-sourcing.md` is portfolio framing with Tier 1/2/3 priorities and Latent inventory snapshot. The data-density asymmetry is *load-bearing* for how each doc gets used at workflow time — brewing docs as cheat-sheet, roasting / sourcing docs as hypothesis-and-priority anchors.
_Avoid_: "WBC reference docs" (close — but Chris's spoken-language phrasing is "reference materials"), "WBC archive" (too narrow — the archive is `wbc-recipes.md` specifically), "WBC corpus" (close, but "corpus" refers to the underlying recipe data, not the docs that derive from it), "WBC research" (close — but research is the *authoring activity*, not the resulting docs), bare "WBC docs" (informal — fine in prose).

**Strategy-zone completeness**:
The principle that Latent's brewing strategy taxonomy should be **legible against the complete known world of strategy zones**, even when most of that world is explicitly not adopted. The principle's purpose is **proactive Motta-prevention** — the WBC reference materials carry a full map of every strategy zone serious competitive brewing employs, so that wrong-zone traps become impossible *to enter* unaware. Chris may decide not to operate in a zone, but he will never not-know-it-exists. Extends the strategy-geography metaphor (strategy = country, sub-form / modifier = state, iteration = city) one level up: the WBC corpus maps the **complete continent of strategy zones**, including the ones Latent currently doesn't visit.

**Awareness vs adoption** — the load-bearing distinction the principle produces. **Awareness surface** = everything mapped in the WBC reference materials (5 foundational control axes + 8 strategy families + 38 subtypes + 102 recipes). **Adoption surface** = Latent's canonical brewing taxonomy (6 strategies + 4 modifiers + 5 Hybrid sub-forms). The gap between them — recorded in `wbc-reference.md § Consciously not pursuing` with explicit per-item reasons — is the **deliberately-not-pursued** set; awareness is universal, adoption is selective. The two halves together cover the full mapped surface.

**Coverage strategy parallels cultivar / terroir** (Chris, 2026-05-16) — the WBC mapping is **comprehensive** (in the canonical-registries Coverage-strategy sense), not tier-scoped, not owned-comprehensive, not self-only. The 102-recipe corpus across 4 competition years × all participants (not just winners) produces enough data density that new WBC routines are expected to map cleanly onto the existing 8 families / 38 subtypes or to be **combinations** of them, rather than introducing truly new families. **Saturation projection** — same asymptotic 95-96% target as the canonical-registries cluster's Pick-not-author principle; new-family-discovery rate decays as competition years accumulate; the mapping converges as the corpus grows.

**Distinct from canonical taxonomies in two ways**: (1) the awareness surface is *external*, not Latent-specific (it maps competitors' work, not Chris's); (2) the canonical adoption decisions (which zones to promote into Latent's strategy enum vs keep awareness-only) happen via **Strategy promotion** (already canonical — v8.4 Hybrid promotion is the precedent), not via the canonical-registries arbiter procedure. Same compounding-knowledge motivation, different operational mechanism.

**Substrate gap is the per-entity analog at the canonical-taxonomies layer** — both name "data exists, but the canonical surface doesn't yet receive it." Substrate gap closes via taxonomy expansion or deliberate scope-out at the entity level (e.g. meso terroir demoted); strategy-zone completeness closes via Strategy promotion or Consciously-not-pursuing at the family/axis level. Different scales, same diagnostic pattern.
_Avoid_: "WBC completeness" (close — but the principle is about *strategy-zone* completeness specifically, not "completeness of the WBC corpus"), "continent mapping" (informal — fine in prose, but the geography metaphor isn't the canonical noun), "wrong-zone-trap prevention" (anchors on the failure mode rather than the principle), "strategy world map" (Chris's spoken phrasing — informal; "strategy-zone completeness" is the canonical noun), "WBC saturation" (overloaded — saturation is a related concept, see canonical-registries Pick-not-author).

**Consciously not pursuing**:
The dedicated `wbc-reference.md` section that records **awareness-locked-but-not-adopted decisions** at the strategy-family / axis / subtype level — the operational form of the Strategy-zone-completeness principle's awareness-vs-adoption gap. Each entry pairs the WBC technique name with the **explicit reason it's not pursued**: hardware overhead, blend stagecraft (no single-origin transfer), out-of-context (heritage brewer modifications), redundant with existing practice (Triangle variable thinking), or coverage decision (Time Distribution as a foundational axis, Filter-Mediated Flow as a foundational axis). The reason is load-bearing — the section exists so the next "should we do this?" question has a recorded answer, and so a future reader knows the omission is deliberate rather than ignorant.

**Doc-section as ADR-substitute** — each "Consciously not pursuing" entry plays the role an ADR file would play for a non-adoption decision, but lives inline in `wbc-reference.md` rather than at `docs/adr/`. The decision *is* hard-to-reverse (re-mapping the taxonomy + back-applying to existing brews is costly), surprising-without-context (a future reader will ask "why doesn't Latent have Time Distribution as a foundational axis when the WBC corpus uses it heavily?"), and the result of a real trade-off — meeting the canonical 3-criteria ADR bar. Kept inline because the section is a natural grouping; promoting individual decisions to `/adr` would scatter related context.

**Promotion-from-not-pursuing is a documented pattern** — entries can move out when Chris's usage justifies it. The v8.5 Role-Based Pulse promotion is the canonical precedent: Time Distribution stayed a foundational-axis non-add (still listed in v8.5's section), but the **Role-Based Pulse sub-case** was promoted from "consciously not pursuing" to a 4th canonical Axis 2 modifier. Same shape as Strategy promotion's modifier → strategy elevation, applied to the awareness → adoption boundary.
_Avoid_: "WBC non-additions" (close — but Chris's phrasing in the doc is "Consciously not pursuing"), "out-of-scope list" (under-specifies the *deliberate* + *with-reasons* framing), "WBC exclusions" (technical but loses the explicit-awareness-but-deliberate-choice nuance), "deferred features" (close — but deferred implies "maybe later"; consciously not pursuing is explicitly "decided no, with a recorded reason — promotion is possible but requires fresh evidence").

**Full-map workflow accessibility** (Chris-locked 2026-05-16) — the operational mandate paired with Consciously-not-pursuing: claude.ai's workflow-authoring process (Coffee Brief construction in particular) must have **MCP read access to the FULL WBC awareness surface**, including the Consciously-not-pursuing section, NOT a pre-filtered view of just Latent's adopted surface. Chris's framing: "I want to make sure the brain and the process for constructing a Coffee Brief is well aware of the whole map and all the zones... it should have access to Google Maps, then go down to where it needs to go, but we shouldn't not give it access to the full map. It should always be aware that it exists." Why this matters: if claude.ai forgets a zone exists (e.g. Time Distribution as a foundational axis), the next Coffee Brief might wrong-zone-trap on a coffee that wants that zone — exactly the Motta failure mode the WBC corpus was authored to prevent. Operationalized today by `wbc-reference.md` being a `docs://` Resource + `read_doc` Tool target with all sections (including Consciously-not-pursuing) intact; future re-organizations of the doc must preserve the full-map shape.

**Foundational control axes**:
The 5-axis analytical decomposition WBC competition routines collectively employ for brewing decisions — Chris's bottoms-up derivation from the 102-recipe corpus during WBC reference materials authoring. The **awareness-surface canonical** for brewing-strategy thinking; distinct from Latent's adopted 2-axis framework (which compresses these 5 into 1 first-class strategy axis + 1 heterogeneous modifier bucket — see Two-Axis Framework for the compression rationale, Strategy-zone completeness for the awareness-vs-adoption framing).

The five axes:

- **Extraction Intensity** — *how much is extracted*. Main levers: grind, ratio, temperature, water chemistry. **Fully absorbed** as Latent's Axis 1 — the 5 intensity strategies (Suppression / Clarity-First / Balanced Intensity / Full Expression / Extraction Push) cover this axis directly. Hybrid is a structural exception (sits on the structural-composition axis but operates with Extraction-Intensity choices inside each phase).
- **Time Distribution** — *when extraction happens*. Main levers: pours, pulse timing, immersion duration. **Partially absorbed**: percolation-only sub-case via the `role_based_pulse` modifier (v8.5 promotion); immersion sub-case via the Phase-Mapped Hybrid sub-form. Remainder (fixed pulse / drain-based pulse / double bloom / short-long-short) lives at doc-layer (Cross-Cutting Control Patterns in `wbc-reference.md`) without first-class promotion — the v8.4 deliberate-non-add reasoning. The **largest under-served axis** — 34 of 102 recipes use Time Distribution as the primary axis.
- **Physical System** — *where / how extraction occurs in the bed*. Main levers: brewer geometry, bed layering, particle-size distribution, grind separation. **Out of scope for Latent** — the Structural Systems family is almost entirely blend stagecraft (24+ recipes are layered beds / dual grinds / blend ratios), doesn't transfer to single-origin home brewing. Consciously not pursuing locks the decision per-pattern with reasons.
- **External Control** — *stabilizing or shaping the process externally*. Main levers: flow tools, thermal handling, agitation devices. **Partially absorbed** as two modifier types: `aroma_capture` (chilling-ball / Paragon for volatile preservation) + `inverted_temperature_staging` (low → high or high → low temp across phases). The `cooling_curve_target` named consideration at Coffee Brief Step 1d touches this axis at a different operational layer (evaluation / service timing, not extraction).
- **Output Selection** — *which parts of extraction are kept*. Main levers: discarding early / late fractions, yield cutoff, post-brew dilution. **Fully absorbed** as the `output_selection` modifier (4 forms post-v8.5: `early_cut` / `late_cut` / `both` / `dilution`). The Selective Bloom Hybrid sub-form is intentionally split off — role assignment, not fraction discarding (see Hybrid sub-form entry).

**Absorption status taxonomy** — three statuses describing each WBC axis's relationship to Latent's adopted surface, the operational form of the awareness-vs-adoption split:

- **Fully absorbed** — Latent's canonical surface covers the WBC axis directly + completely. Today: Extraction Intensity (Axis 1) + Output Selection (output_selection modifier).
- **Partially absorbed** — Latent canonical covers a sub-set of the WBC axis; remainder lives at doc-layer (Cross-Cutting Control Patterns) for awareness without first-class promotion. Today: Time Distribution + External Control.
- **Out of scope** — WBC axis mapped in awareness (Strategy-zone completeness) but adoption deliberately not pursued. Today: Physical System.

**The translation layer IS the architecture, not a hack** (Chris-locked 2026-05-16). Latent's 4 modifier types map structurally 1:1 onto WBC axes 2-5 (Output Selection ↔ `output_selection`; External Control ↔ `aroma_capture` + `inverted_temperature_staging`; Time Distribution ↔ `role_based_pulse` + Phase-Mapped Hybrid; Physical System ↔ out-of-scope). Latent represents the same information content as 1 strategy axis + 1 typed bag, rather than 5 separate first-class axes. The 5-axis adoption was deliberately rejected because (a) 3 of the 5 axes (Physical System / Time Distribution / External Control) would be empty or single-valued on most brews — exactly the **category bloat** failure mode (separate entry); (b) **Strategy promotion** already exists as the operational mechanism for moving sub-axes from awareness to adoption when usage justifies (v8.4 Hybrid, v8.5 Role-Based Pulse); (c) Strategy-zone completeness already gives the awareness floor without forcing schema expansion.

**Promotion authority is Chris-driven, not system-driven** (paired with Strategy promotion's existing rules) — promoting a WBC axis or family from awareness to adoption is the human operator's judgment call, NOT claude.ai's authoring decision and NOT Claude Code's arbiter decision. The mapping itself (which WBC axis lands where in Latent) is system vocabulary; the **promotion timing** is Chris's call. Concretely: claude.ai may surface "this brew's framing routinely reaches for Time Distribution moves the modifier system absorbs awkwardly" as a doc-proposal observation, but the decision to promote (e.g. add `time_distribution` as a first-class axis) is Chris's per-sprint scoping call after enough cross-coffee pattern accumulates.

_Avoid_: "WBC 5-axis taxonomy" (close — fine in prose; "Foundational control axes" is the canonical noun from `wbc-reference.md`), "WBC axes" (under-specified — could mean 5 foundational or 8 family), "control axes" (bare — overloaded against generic control-system meaning), "brewing axes" (under-specified — Latent's 2 axes are also brewing axes), "axes" without qualifier (always pin "foundational" or "Latent's two" so the layer is unambiguous).

**Absorption status**:
The per-axis classification of each WBC Foundational control axis's relationship to Latent's adopted brewing taxonomy — three values (**fully absorbed** / **partially absorbed** / **out of scope**) that together name the awareness-vs-adoption gap operationally. Distinct from the canonical-registries cluster's **Aggregation-eligibility** (page-bearing / page-deferred / validation-only) which classifies *axes' relationship to knowledge aggregation*; same per-axis-status shape, different decision. Distinct from the canonical-registries cluster's **Coverage strategy** (comprehensive / tier-scoped / owned-comprehensive / self-only) which classifies *how far a registry tries to reach into a domain*; Coverage strategy describes registry extent, Absorption status describes Latent-canonical-surface coverage of an external taxonomy. **The pattern generalizes** — any future imported taxonomy (e.g. the SCA tasting-protocol vocabulary, an alternative roasting school's terminology) would also use Absorption status as its translation surface; today's only instance is the WBC Foundational control axes mapping.
_Avoid_: "axis status" (under-specified — many things have status; absorption-into-Latent is the specific framing), "mapping status" (close — but mapping is what produces absorption status, not the status itself), "coverage status" (overloaded against Coverage strategy), "adoption level" (close — but adoption is the binary boundary; the per-axis status carries 3 values + the partially-absorbed middle is the load-bearing one).

**Sourcing priority**:
The WBC-corpus-derived 3-value classification of green-bean lots for **buying decisions** — a "soft guiding post" (Chris-locked 2026-05-16) for sourcing, NOT a canonical-validation surface. Lives in [wbc-sourcing.md § 7](../../docs/roasting/wbc-sourcing.md). Three values, each with a heuristic green-bean shape:

- **T1 — Best Fit** — cleanest-fit for the dominant WBC competition palate. Examples: washed Panama Gesha, white honey Gesha (Colombia or Panama), clean natural Panama Gesha, Bolivia washed Gesha / Takesi-style, washed or clean honey Chiroso, clean Sidra, Sudan Rume washed / controlled natural.
- **T2 — High Learning Value** — high-information lots that teach how cultivar / process / roast interact. Examples: Mikava CM Gesha, CGLE Mandela / CGLE 17, Inmaculada Sudan Rume / Eugenioides, Janson natural Gesha, Finca Deborah washed / hybrid Gesha, Las Flores Java / Chiroso.
- **T3 — Buy Selectively** — high-intensity competition coffees that can become stylized or process-forward. Examples: thermal-shock Wilton Benitez-style coffees, heavy anaerobic natural Gesha, Eugenioides standalone, Liberica blends, process-heavy Ombligon.

**Naming-clash disambiguation against Producer Reference role tier** (Chris-locked 2026-05-16) — both schemes use Tier 1/2/3 numbering, but they classify different things:
- **Producer Reference role tier** (Anchor / Signal / Experimental) — names the producer's **calibration purpose** in Chris's research-and-aggregation system. Determines how much registry content gets authored per producer + the producer's role in cross-coffee aggregation. Author-side / taxonomy-build decision.
- **Sourcing priority** (T1 Best Fit / T2 Learning / T3 Selective) — names the green-bean lot's **buying priority** against the WBC-palate target. Author-time decision is irrelevant; this is a recurring buy-decision input. WBC-research byproduct.

The two schemes are **orthogonal** — a T1 Anchor producer (e.g. CGLE) can produce T2-Learning sourcing-priority greens (Sudan Rume Natural learning lot) AND T3-Selective sourcing-priority greens (heavy anaerobic experimental) AND historically T1-Best-Fit greens (clean washed lots) — same producer, three different sourcing priorities depending on the green. Reference role classifies the *producer*; Sourcing priority classifies the *lot*. The historical naming overlap was incidental — Chris's intent was never to lockstep them; the WBC sourcing tier was renamed Sourcing priority during the 2026-05-16 canonical-registries / WBC-cluster grilling to make the disambiguation explicit.

**Latent-adjusted sourcing priority** — the re-ranked reading after applying Chris's *actual* palate (VERY-expressive + Suppression-leaning) against the WBC-palate-keyed raw tiers. Under the adjustment:
- **T1 (raw)** is **important but not urgent** — clean clarity-Gesha is over-indexed in specialty coffee right now and not Chris's current focus, BUT see Skill-maintenance lane (separate entry) for why the lane still earns periodic buying.
- **T2 (raw)** is **aligned with current focus** — roast-learning hybrids (Sudan Rume / Mandela / CGLE 17 / Java) are already core to Latent's recent inventory.
- **T3 (raw)** is **more aligned than the WBC framing suggests** — controlled high-process coffees suit the "expressive + Suppression" stance better than the raw-WBC framing implies.

The adjustment is per-decision and re-applied at each buying moment; today's snapshot in `wbc-sourcing.md § Portfolio gap analysis (Latent-adjusted)` uses the Latent-adjusted reading for next-buy recommendations.

**Soft guiding post, not validation** — `green_beans` writes do not validate against Sourcing priority. The tier is an advisory frame for Chris's buying judgment + claude.ai's sourcing-related Coffee Brief context, not an enforcement layer. The 3 values are not a canonical registry; they're an analytical framework with worked examples.
_Avoid_: "WBC sourcing tier" (legacy noun, breaks the Producer Reference role clash — renamed Sourcing priority during 2026-05-16 grilling), "buying tier" (close — but tier overloads against Reference role tier; "priority" makes the orthogonality explicit), "sourcing target" (under-specified — every prospective buy is a sourcing target; priority is the per-target tier rating), "WBC tier" (under-specified — could mean Reference role for producers, Sourcing priority for greens, or Tier 1/2/3 experiment queues for brewing / roasting).

**Skill-maintenance lane**:
An adopted strategy zone or coffee style where Chris's *personal preference* pulls away from regular practice, but **periodic practice is maintained explicitly to prevent the zone from becoming a blind spot**. Sits between regular-adoption (in the awareness-vs-adoption frame from Strategy-zone completeness) and Consciously-not-pursuing — Chris knows this lane exists, hasn't deliberately scoped it out, and is choosing to *practice it periodically* even though it isn't where his current focus naturally pulls.

**Canonical instance** — the **clean clarity-Gesha roasting lane**. Chris's framing (2026-05-16): "the clean clarity-Gesha type coffees, I do have a little bit of a blind spot towards. And even though maybe I may lean towards more funkier process suppression-type stuff, I really do need to do a whole green-bean lot iteration exercise around normal clean Geisha type stuff because that is so represented on the WBC scene. It can't be a blind spot for me even though that might not necessarily lean towards my personal direct preference." The WBC corpus is *heavy* on washed Panama Gesha and clean clarity coffees — they dominate the dataset; maintaining roasting skill on this lane keeps championship-mode readiness viable. The wbc-roasting.md framing names the cadence: "A reference clean-Gesha lot every 2-3 buying cycles keeps the lane practiced."

**Distinct from Consciously not pursuing** — Consciously not pursuing is "decided NO with a recorded reason"; Skill-maintenance is "decided YES periodically, with the natural pull elsewhere." Different boundary on the same Strategy-zone-completeness map.

**Distinct from regular adoption** — regular adoption follows organic interest; skill-maintenance is deliberate counter-pull practice. Without the explicit framing, skill-maintenance lanes naturally drift toward becoming blind spots over time because new lots / brews / experiments default to where preference points.

**Generalizes beyond clean-Gesha** — any zone the WBC corpus surfaces as load-bearing for championship-mode skill but where Chris's preference naturally pulls away is a candidate. Today's only locked instance is clean clarity-Gesha; future candidates could include specific brewing strategies (e.g. a Clarity-First brewing skill-maintenance if Suppression dominates Chris's recent brews) or specific roast intents (e.g. fast counterflow on a particular cultivar lane).

**Operational mechanism is sourcing-time** — skill-maintenance lanes earn their place via the buying cycle. `wbc-sourcing.md § Best next sourcing moves` carries item 6: "Clean washed Panama Gesha — schedule for a future cycle to keep the clean clarity-Gesha roast lane practiced; not the urgent buy." That's the operational form — periodic buying at a relaxed cadence, not aggressive sourcing.
_Avoid_: "blind spot" (the *failure mode* the lane prevents, not the lane itself), "practice lane" (under-specified — could mean any practice cadence), "maintenance lane" (close — but skill-maintenance pins the *why*; the maintenance is specifically about skill retention against natural-preference drift), "secondary lane" (close — but secondary implies a hierarchy; skill-maintenance is parallel to primary focus, not below), "discipline lane" (close — but discipline implies effort against resistance; skill-maintenance is more periodic-rotation than ongoing-discipline).

**Portfolio lanes**:
The 5-lane portfolio-construction frame Chris uses for **green-bean inventory balance** — distinct from Sourcing priority (which classifies per-lot buying priority). The 5 lanes name the **role-shape** a balanced inventory should cover, regardless of which individual lots fill each lane. Lives in [wbc-sourcing.md § 10](../../docs/roasting/wbc-sourcing.md). Formalized 5-lane authored shape locked Sprint T2 (2026-05-18) after living as a 4-lane authored shape + implicit-5th-via-gap-analysis between 2026-05-09 and 2026-05-18.

- **Reference clarity** — clean clarity-Gesha-style. Examples: washed Panama Gesha, Bolivia Gesha, clean Ethiopia 74158.
- **Fruit-tea expression** — clean natural / honey-process with fruit-forward + tea-like character. Examples: natural Panama Gesha, white honey Gesha, clean Sidra.
- **Process learning** — high-process-intervention coffees for cultivar / process / roast interaction learning. Examples: CM Gesha, mossto washed, cold-fermented natural.
- **Roast-learning hybrids** — Gesha-alternative hybrids whose roast behavior teaches across cultivar lineages. Examples: Mandela, Sudan Rume, Java, Chiroso, CGLE 17.
- **Value / roast-practice** — sub-$30/kg cheap experiment substrate for 3-batch dev ladders + rest-curve experiments + green-curve calibration without burning expensive lots on basic-skill iterations. Examples: washed Bourbon / Caturra; value-tier Brazil / Guatemala / Honduras washed. Eats fast at 100g/batch — even a 5-pound value lot supports ~22 practice roasts, which the iteration cadence consumes quickly enough to matter (see Sourcing constraints).

**Portfolio gap analysis** — the operational practice of mapping current inventory against the 5-lane frame to surface missing lanes. Runs at each inventory-change moment (new green purchase, lot close-out, archive). Today's worked example is `wbc-sourcing.md § Latent inventory mapped to tiers` (2026-05-09 snapshot) which calls out:
- Reference clarity: **off-pattern only** (Bukure Red Bourbon; no active washed Panama Gesha)
- Fruit-tea expression: **reasonable coverage** (GESHA CLOUDS)
- Process learning: **well-covered** (El Paraíso + Higuito + Wush Wush + Sudan Rume Natural)
- Roast-learning hybrids: **partial coverage** (Sudan Rume only; no Mandela / CGLE 17 / Sidra / Chiroso / Java active)
- Value / roast-practice: **real gap** (no active sub-$30/kg practice coffee)

**Distinct from Process lanes A / B / C** (in `wbc-sourcing.md § 4`) — Process lanes A/B/C classify *processing intent* (Lane A clean / Lane B learning / Lane C high-risk). The two frames overlap (a Process-Lane-A coffee usually fills the Reference-clarity Portfolio lane), but aren't identical — Process-Lane-C high-risk coffees usually fill the Process-learning Portfolio lane; Fruit-tea-expression and Roast-learning-hybrids Portfolio lanes have no clean Process-lane mapping. Portfolio lanes is the portfolio-construction frame; Process lanes A/B/C is the process-intent classification orthogonal to portfolio role.

**Distinct from Skill-maintenance lane** — Skill-maintenance lane is a *kind* of adopted zone (clean clarity-Gesha being the canonical example); Portfolio lanes is the inventory-shape frame. They intersect — the Reference-clarity Portfolio lane is largely the Skill-maintenance lane in operational practice — but Portfolio lanes is the higher-level umbrella covering all 5 role-shapes.
_Avoid_: "lanes" without qualifier (now overloaded across Skill-maintenance lane + Process lanes A/B/C + Portfolio lanes — always pin which), "inventory lanes" (close — but Portfolio lanes is the canonical noun matching wbc-sourcing.md § 10), "buy lanes" (under-specified — could mean any sourcing decomposition), "portfolio buckets" (informal — fine in prose), "portfolio slots" (close — slot suggests fixed shape; lane suggests parallel paths through inventory shape).

**Sourcing constraints**:
The physical and structural realities that bound Chris's green-bean buying — the **substrate the Sourcing priority + Portfolio lanes + (future) Risk-tier sourcing frames all operate against**. Three layers:

- **Roest L200 100g-per-batch capacity** — every roast is 100g; a 1-pound (454g) lot supports ~4-5 roasts; a 5-pound (~2.3kg) lot supports ~22-23 roasts. Lots below 1 pound burn through too fast to support V-set iteration; lots above 5 pounds overflow practical storage + freeze capacity for a single-person operation.
- **1-5 pound purchase window** — practical upper and lower bound on standard lot size. Below 1 pound = not enough iterations to learn anything from (Chris's framing: "I want enough iterations to learn something from"); above 5 pounds = unsold green sits indefinitely ("I'm not selling it"). **One-shot lots** (100-120g auction samples, separate canonical entry) are the explicit exception to the lower bound, with dedicated routing through one-shot prompts + the `green_beans.is_one_shot` flag.
- **Individual-not-commercial scale** — Chris buys for personal championship-mode research, not for a roaster business. The volume + access patterns of importer / exporter relationships keyed to commercial buyers (typically 50-200kg orders, multi-month contracts) don't apply; access patterns must be hobbyist / specialty / direct-relationship-keyed, not commercial.

**The Tier 1 producer access paradox** (Chris-locked 2026-05-16) — Reference-role Tier 1 Anchor producers (CGLE, Janson, Mikava, Finca Deborah, Hacienda La Esmeralda) have the *highest cup ceiling* AND the *deepest pre-existing roaster relationships* AND the *largest typical export volumes*. Their best lots are largely contracted to top-tier roasters before any visible market access; the importer / exporter channels that do carry them sell in volumes incompatible with the 1-5lb window. **Direct relationships are the only viable access path** to Tier 1 producer green at single-person scale — which makes Sourcing channels (separate entry) load-bearing in a way the Sourcing priority / WBC tier framework doesn't acknowledge: being able to *buy* a coffee is a separate problem from being able to *want* a coffee. Chris's World of Coffee 2026 trip was explicitly to break the access constraint — outcomes included the CGLE direct WhatsApp thread, Forest Coffee relationship (Forrest sells Milton Monroy's GESHA CLOUDS), and small specialty competition-grade importers (Jah Coffee / Showroom Coffee / Untold Coffee Lab / Forward Coffee) — see Sourcing channel entry.

**Why the constraints matter for the rest of the system** — the Sourcing-constraints layer is *why* the Portfolio gap analysis surfaces a value / roast-practice gap as load-bearing (cheap experiment substrate gets eaten quickly at 100g/batch and the practice cadence is what keeps more-expensive lots from being burned on basic-skill iterations); *why* the Risk-tier sourcing decomposition exists (Chris can only afford a small number of high-risk lots per buying cycle without compromising learning velocity); and *why* the long-term competition-grade-access trajectory matters (the producer-relationship building is the multi-year unlock that gradually moves Tier 1 producer access from impossible to viable).
_Avoid_: "buying constraints" (close — but buying frames the buyer-side; "sourcing" carries the bilateral relationship-channel reality), "sourcing limits" (under-specified — limits suggests maxima only; constraints carry both minima and maxima + the access-paradox layer), "Roest constraints" (under-specified — the 100g capacity is one of three layers), "scale constraints" (close — but scale doesn't carry the relationship-access paradox), "physical constraints" (close — but physical doesn't carry the commercial-vs-individual structural layer).

**Risk-tier sourcing**:
Chris's operational 3-tier classification of green-bean lots by **roast-execution risk** at buy time — distinct from Sourcing priority (WBC-palate fit) and Producer Reference role (calibration purpose). The risk tier names *how confident Chris is in producing a workable roast given current skill + carry-forward learnings*; it determines how much green is reasonable to commit per buying decision.

- **Lower-risk learning lot** — easier-to-handle, more general, building base roasting knowledge. Provides iteration practice substrate. Tractable on first attempt with normal V-set framing.
- **Higher-risk learning lot** — complex amazing-cup potential, might mis-execute, but acceptable because still in skill-building stage. Cup ceiling worth the iteration risk. Standard V-set framing but with widened V1 spread + close attention to carry-forward anchors.
- **One-shot competition lot** — riskiest tier; 100-120g auction sample, single roast, no recovery possible (see one-shot lot canonical entry). Requires Tolerance-anchored design (already canonical) with a tight carry-forward anchor; no margin for iteration.

**Familiarity de-risking** (Chris-articulated 2026-05-16) — risk tiers are NOT static per coffee; they **decay over time as carry-forward learnings compound**. Each repeat exposure to a (cultivar / process / producer / variety) dimension narrows the future risk on coffees sharing those dimensions. **Worked example**: CGLE Sudan Rume Washed + CGLE Sudan Rume Natural already roasted → next Sudan Rume from any producer becomes less risky (cultivar familiarity) → next CGLE Sudan Rume is less risky still (cultivar + producer + relationship familiarity). The mechanism is just **carry-forward learnings** (already canonical) applied to the sourcing-decision layer rather than the roast-design layer. **The compounding direction is the load-bearing call** — competition-grade-access-trajectory is the long-term, familiarity-de-risking is the short-term mechanism that makes the trajectory traversable.

**Compounding-knowledge is the explicit goal at the system level** (Chris's framing: "knowledge compounds so I get much closer in calibration to all of these things. And that also is the goal — one of the main goals of the Latent system too"). Sourcing-side familiarity de-risking is the Latent-system-design philosophy applied to the buying surface, not a separate practice.
_Avoid_: "buying tier" (overloads against Sourcing priority + Producer Reference role tier; "risk-tier" is the operative axis), "lot risk" (close — but lot risk is what risk-tier-sourcing measures, not the practice itself), "execution risk" (close — but execution-risk is one component; risk-tier carries the buy-decision framing), bare "risk tier" (under-specified — risk tiers exist in many contexts; pin "sourcing"), "compounding-de-risk" (Chris's verbal phrasing — informal; canonical is "familiarity de-risking"), "calibration compounding" (close — but calibration is one *outcome* of familiarity de-risking; the noun is the de-risking itself).

**Sourcing channel**:
The **path / relationship through which a green-bean lot is acquired** — the operational form of the Tier-1-producer-access-paradox layer in Sourcing constraints. Five kinds today, each characterized by volume + access pattern + relationship depth + competition-grade compatibility:

- **Generalist retailer** — broad catalog hobbyist-friendly volumes. Sweet Maria's is the canonical example. Access pattern is anonymous + non-relational; volume is open (any size). Useful for early skill-building lots; rare to find competition-grade content.
- **Specialty importer** — small curated catalog, hand-selected, hobbyist-friendly volumes. Examples: Jah Coffee, Showroom Coffee. Access pattern semi-anonymous; volumes typically 1-5lb. Bridges generalist + competition-grade access.
- **Competition-grade importer** — niche catalog focused on competition-grade lots, often single-person-run or small specialty operations. Examples: Untold Coffee Lab, Forward Coffee (Panama-based). Smaller catalogs, higher-quality-per-listing, more relationship-keyed. Critical channel for accessing competition-grade green at single-person scale.
- **Direct-from-farm** — relationship-keyed channel with the producer directly. Examples: CGLE (WhatsApp thread post-relationship-building), Forest Coffee (Milton Monroy / GESHA CLOUDS source post-World-of-Coffee), Gesha Village (sells 1kg sample bags directly via website). **Sub-pattern: farms selling 1kg-ish bags directly to end consumers** — when available, the ideal channel (highest cup ceiling + hobbyist-compatible volume); not all farms do it. The Tier-1-producer-access-paradox's primary unlock.
- **Auction-sample channel** — auction-lot sample sets, farm-direct sample sets sent during sourcing negotiations, rare allocations from limited drops. 100-120g single-batch volumes — the one-shot-lot sourcing pipeline (see one-shot lot canonical entry).
- **Direct-from-auction** (awareness-only today, Chris-articulated 2026-05-16) — direct purchase of full auction lots, typically through friends or contacts who participate in auctions. Highest-end access path AND highest volumes; auction-lot quantities are typically incompatible with the Sourcing-constraints 1-5lb window. **Awareness-locked, not currently adopted** — Chris doesn't bid on full auction lots today; future scope as relationship network grows.

**Geisha Village classification correction** (Chris-locked 2026-05-16) — Geisha Village was initially classified as a generalist retailer because it sells via consumer-facing website, but is structurally a **direct-from-farm** channel: high-end farm itself, sells 1kg sample bags directly. The classification corrected during 2026-05-16 grilling.

**Competition-grade access trajectory**:
The long-term producer-relationship-building progression Chris pursues to gradually unlock the highest-end competition-grade green at single-person scale. The trajectory moves the buying mix from **generalist-retailer + specialty-importer** dominant (skill-building stage, today's secondary mix) toward **direct-from-farm + competition-grade-importer + direct-from-auction** dominant (championship-mode stage, multi-year horizon). Pairs with Familiarity de-risking on the short term: as accumulated cultivar / process / producer / variety experience narrows execution risk, Chris can take on higher-end + riskier lots without compromising learning velocity.

**Operational mechanisms** for advancing the trajectory:
- **Coffee industry events** — World of Coffee (Chris's 2026 attendance produced the CGLE direct WhatsApp + Forest Coffee + Jah / Showroom / Untold / Forward relationships), cupping events with roasters, specialty conferences. Direct in-person rapport is the canonical relationship-opener.
- **Cupping with named roasters** — face-to-face cupping events where Chris meets head roasters (the Special Guests Coffee event where Chris cupped CGLE Sudan Rume Natural with the head roaster). Opens calibration-pair availability (see Calibration pair entry).
- **Relationship maintenance** — once a direct channel is open (CGLE WhatsApp, Forest Coffee email), continued buying + communication keeps the channel viable for future high-end allocations.
- **ProducerEntry.contact field** — the structured carrier of the relationship state at the canonical-registries layer; rich-registry's only relationship-aware field. Records the social-media handle / email / WhatsApp through which the producer is reachable. See Producer sourcing surface (already canonical) for the second-order role producer registry plays as a relationship network.

The trajectory's end-state is **direct competition-grade access** — Chris being a recognized small-scale researcher whose green requests reach Tier-1 producers directly, with allocations sized for 1-5lb individual scale. Not achievable in one or two years; multi-year horizon.
_Avoid_: "sourcing path" (close — but channel is the canonical noun matching wbc-sourcing.md framing), "buying relationship" (under-specified — relationship is one component; channel covers the path + relationship + volume + access-pattern bundle), "supply channel" (close — but supply is industry-flavored; sourcing is the Latent-canonical verb), "import channel" (under-specified — direct-from-farm and direct-from-auction aren't import channels), bare "channel" (overloaded — many things are channels; pin "sourcing").

**Calibration pair**:
A sourcing practice Chris uses to **anchor his interpretation of a green-bean lot** against an existing roasted expression of the same lot — the **pairing** of (green bean lot, roasted bean from a known roaster or the producer themselves) acquired together for calibration. Specifically Chris-articulated 2026-05-16, flagged for inclusion as a standing sourcing-prompt practice (paired follow-up item).

**Worked example** — CGLE Sudan Rume Natural: (1) Chris cupped the coffee at an event with the head roaster from Special Guests Coffee (face-to-face calibration data point); (2) Chris bought the roasted version of that specific lot from Special Guests (a structured roaster expression of the green); (3) Chris bought the raw green lot from CGLE direct (his own roasting input). The three together produce a **multi-anchor calibration baseline**:
- **Producer's tasting notes** (already canonical via `green_beans.producer_tasting_notes`) — external ballpark anchor.
- **Known roaster's interpretation** — one validated expression of what the green CAN be at competition-roast quality (when sourced from a Reference-role-Tier-1-Anchor or known-style roaster).
- **Chris's brewing of the roaster's roasted bean** — Chris's own consumption-condition cup of the roaster's expression; calibrates Chris's brewing layer against the roaster's roasting layer.
- **Chris's own roast** — the target of the V-set work, to be compared against the multi-anchor baseline.

**Massively accelerates dialing in his own roast of the green** — collapses the design search space substantially. Without a calibration pair, V1 design is anchored only on producer notes + carry-forward learnings from similar cultivar / terroir / process lots (which may not match this specific producer's processing nuances). With a calibration pair, Chris knows what the lot is *capable of* in a competition-roast hands, and his V-set work is directly comparable against a known target.

**Not always available** — depends on finding a roaster who's bought + roasted the specific green lot Chris is also buying. The intersection of "I'm buying this green" + "a roaster I trust roasted this green" + "the roaster's roasted bean is still purchasable" is narrow. When available, deliberately sought; when not, V1 design falls back on producer notes + carry-forward learnings only.

**Pairs with face-to-face cupping at events** — the highest-fidelity calibration data point. Cupping with the head roaster at an event adds palate-calibration metadata that can't be reconstructed from the bag-only purchase later. The Special Guests Coffee + CGLE Sudan Rume Natural example combined all three: event cupping with the head roaster + bag purchase of the roasted version + green-bean lot from CGLE directly.

**Open follow-up** — Chris flagged 2026-05-16 that calibration-pair seeking should become part of his explicit green-bean-sourcing routine. Today it happens opportunistically when available; the operational mandate is to *actively search for the pair* when buying competition-grade lots, since the calibration uplift is high enough to justify the additional search cost.
_Avoid_: "roasted-cup pairing" (descriptive but loses the *calibration* function framing), "roaster reference" (close — but a Reference role tier is something else; calibration pair is the matched-green-and-roasted instance, not a producer tier), "double sourcing" (informal; doesn't carry the calibration purpose), "reference roast pair" (overloaded — reference roast is the lot-level winner inside Latent; calibration pair is the external matched-pair from a different roaster's reference roast on the same green), "matched pair" (under-specified — what's matched?).

**Cross-cutting control patterns**:
The `wbc-reference.md § Cross-Cutting Control Patterns` doc-layer surface that captures **control areas surfaced repeatedly across the 102-recipe corpus but deliberately NOT promoted to canonical Axis 2 modifiers** — the "applied + recorded via free-text `strategy_notes`, not validated against a canonical surface" state on the awareness-vs-adoption gradient. Distinct from canonical modifier types (which validate writes), Consciously not pursuing (explicit non-adoption with reasons), and Practical experiment queue (candidates queued for future promotion). Chris's v8.5 explicit framing: "keep compact strategy set, add separate doc layer."

**Five patterns today**, each with a per-pattern Chris-relationship-status (locked 2026-05-16):

- **Time Distribution Practical Playbook** (5 templates: fixed pulse / role-based pulse / drain-based pulse / double bloom / short-long-short) — **borderline-canonical**. Chris already practices much of this via SWORKS valve work + Phase-Mapped Hybrid sub-form; the playbook may earn promotion to a canonical Axis 2 modifier in a future sprint. Open follow-up for Strategy-promotion review.
- **Water Strength** (mineral content 20-160ppm as strategic control, including staged ppm across pours) — **short-medium-term active experiment area**. Chris's explicit commitment 2026-05-16; not yet executed but high-priority queue.
- **Agitation Taper** (high → low agitation across pours; saturation/sweetness early, finish-clarity protection late) — **collapses to Role-Based Pulse with taper-naming roles**. When Agitation Taper is the recipe-defining move, the canonical `role_based_pulse` modifier's `roles` field describes the taper rather than treating Agitation Taper as a separate concept. Already canonical in this collapsed form.
- **Filter Behavior** (filter as texture + extraction-shape variable beyond fast/slow tagging) — **explicit measurement plan** parallel to EG-1 grinder enumeration. Chris's commitment 2026-05-16: measure true output flow per owned filter, similar to the EG-1's 51-enumerated-settings approach. Resolves the long-standing approximate-not-measured filter taxonomy gap (already flagged in canonical-registries cluster).
- **Pre-Brew Conditioning** (post-grind homogenization, pre-ground rest 10-30 minutes, humidity / nitrogen storage / cold grinding) — **lower priority but possible**. Chris has the equipment for the easy variants (post-grind homogenization, pre-ground rest); humidity / nitrogen / cold grinding deferred to Consciously not pursuing per cost / repeatability friction.

**The patterns persist via `strategy_notes`** — `brews.strategy_notes` is the canonical free-text overflow column where Cross-cutting control pattern application gets recorded per-brew when relevant. The recording IS the state — applied + noted + not validated. Distinct from `modifiers` (the canonical-validated jsonb) and from canonical strategy fields (the validated enum).

**Output Selection's relationship is different** — Output Selection is *fully canonical* as a modifier (4 forms post-v8.5: `early_cut` / `late_cut` / `both` / `dilution`). It appears in Cross-cutting control patterns as "Output Selection (extended)" with the broader WBC nomenclature mapped onto the canonical forms, but is NOT a cross-cutting pattern in the unpromoted sense. Chris's 2026-05-16 framing: this is "one of the more unique things I also came up from first principles" — the most natural-leaning of the WBC alignments, already in active use.
_Avoid_: "cross-cutting patterns" (under-specified — many things cross-cut; pin "control patterns"), "doc-layer patterns" (close — but doc-layer is the *state*, not the patterns themselves), "non-canonical patterns" (close — but the patterns ARE canonical at the doc layer, just not at the validation-mirror layer), "free-text patterns" (informal — strategy_notes is the carrier, not the canonical noun), "playbook patterns" (close — playbook is what wbc-reference.md uses for the umbrella; Cross-cutting control patterns is the precise noun for the 5-area structure).

**Experiment status** (renamed from "Practical experiment queue Tier 1/2/3"):
The classification of candidate experiments surfaced by the WBC corpus — the **queued state** on the awareness-vs-adoption gradient between Cross-cutting control patterns (applied at doc-layer) and Consciously not pursuing (explicit non-adoption). Renamed from Tier 1/2/3 during 2026-05-16 grilling to break the cumulative naming clash with Producer Reference role tier + Sourcing priority tier — Chris's framing: "you don't have to keep it as tier one, tier two, tier three. I don't know why I always gravitate towards calling everything tier one, tier two, tier three." Two active values + a third that redirects to Consciously not pursuing:

- **Active** (formerly "Tier 1 — test now") — high-signal, low-effort candidate experiments queued for near-term execution. Brewing-side actives (`wbc-reference.md § Practical Experiment Queue`): double bloom on fast papers, output cut test, post-brew dilution, agitation taper (now canonical via `role_based_pulse`), water strength ladder, filter behavior test, pre-ground rest. Roasting-side actives (`wbc-roasting.md § Roest experiment queue`): rest curve on reference roast, same-green dev ladder (the 3-batch ladder), ground vs whole Agtron logging, mid-phase build for dense hybrids, aroma capture on freeze.
- **Future-capture** (formerly "Tier 2") — interesting but lower priority. Could-do-easily-but-deprioritized state (Chris's 2026-05-16 walk-through surfaced multiple cases: mid-pour temperature blending — has the kettles, just lower priority; roast-based structuring on single origin — already self-roasting, lower priority than other queue items). Brewing-side future-captures: mid-pour temperature blending, roast-based structuring, layered bed by component, dual chamber / wet-blended extraction, silk / hydrophobic filter materials. Roasting-side future-captures: screen-size pre-roast separation, multi-machine split-roast, multi-process blending across two greens.
- **(Not-pursuing — redirects to Consciously not pursuing)** — the third value collapses to the existing Consciously-not-pursuing canonical concept; included here for completeness of the queue's 3-tier source structure but not a separate Experiment status value.

**Naming-clash discipline** (Chris-locked 2026-05-16) — the cumulative Tier 1/2/3 systems now read as: Producer Reference role tier (Anchor / Signal / Experimental), Sourcing priority (Best Fit / Learning / Selective), and Experiment status (Active / Future-capture). All three use different vocabulary deliberately; "tier" was retired from the experiment-queue surface to keep the naming surface untangled. Future schemes that surface 3-tier patterns should follow the same discipline — pick descriptive value names, not Tier 1/2/3.

**Promotion-from-queue is documented** — Active experiments that produce confirmable cross-coffee signal can be promoted from queue → Cross-cutting control pattern → canonical modifier. The v8.5 Role-Based Pulse promotion is the canonical precedent: was Tier 1 Active in v8.4 → promoted to canonical Axis 2 modifier in v8.5. The Filter Behavior measurement plan is the next candidate — once flow rates are measured per filter, filter taxonomy gets enriched (canonical-registries cluster handles the registry-update path) and the Active status closes.
_Avoid_: "Practical experiment queue Tier 1/2/3" (legacy phrasing; renamed to break the tier-clash), "experiment tier" (overloads against Reference role / Sourcing priority tiers), "experiment priority" (close — but priority overloads against Sourcing priority), "queue status" (under-specified — the queue carries status as one of its dimensions, not the dimension itself), "test priority" (under-specified — testing is one mode; status carries the broader queue-state framing).

**Same-green blending**:
The umbrella WBC-derived experiment shape for **single-lot blending experiments** — three variants that all operate on one green lot without requiring multi-origin sourcing. The deliberate Latent-scope alternative to multi-origin blend stagecraft (which lives in Consciously not pursuing). Lives in [wbc-roasting.md § Blending experiments](../../docs/roasting/wbc-roasting.md). Chris's framing: "the most direct WBrC lesson for Roest work."

Three variants:

- **Same-green roast layering** (development split) — 3 batches at differential development / drop levels from one green lot. Canonical Roest L200 protocol: Batch A floral clarity (fast counterflow, shortest clean dev, ~9-10% dev, earliest acceptable color drop); Batch B fruit + sweetness (same profile but slightly more late Maillard / slightly longer dev, ~11-12% dev or +1-2°C drop); Batch C structure (slightly more development or higher drop, still light, ~12-14% dev or +2-4°C drop). The day-7 evaluation produces a **blend matrix** of 6 cups: A alone / B alone / C alone / 70%B+30%A / 70%B+30%C / 50%A+50%C. Same pourover recipe + same rest day + ground Agtron tracking per component. WBC precedents: George Peng 2025 1st (3 dev levels, single Mount Totumas Gesha), Raul Rodas 2025 (Stronghold + Link split on Finca El Injerto Gesha), Barry McGeehin 2025 (50/50 Stronghold + Link split on Esmeralda Ellipse).
- **Same-green Agtron-paired blending** (color-targeted split) — two roasts at deliberately different Agtron readings (e.g. 80 + 90 or 70 + 90) from one green lot, blended to test whether color-paired layering outperforms a single mid-color roast. Daiki Hatakeyama 2025 pattern (Agtron 80 sweet aroma + Agtron 90 sweet taste, 1:1).
- **Same-green rest split** (rest-window blend) — two rest windows on the same roast (e.g. 14 days + 3 days) blended to test rest-window layering. Barry McGeehin 2025 pattern (14 days Stronghold + 3 days Link, same coffee).

**Green-quantity gating**: 2000g+ remaining = full 3-batch ladder + blend matrix; 1000-2000g = ladder but meaningful fraction of green; 500-1000g = tight, consider 2-batch (A vs C) split; <500g = single reference roast only, defer blending to a future lot. Operationalized via `list_roest_inventory` MCP Tool — check inventory before scoping the ladder.

**Structural overlap with V-set framing**: same-green blending is a V-set at the design level (1-4 batches from one green, each with specific intent), but the EVALUATION step diverges — V-sets evaluate batch slots against each other to designate a leading slot; same-green blending evaluates against the blend matrix to identify the best combination (which may be a blend rather than a single batch). The experiment frame's `primary_question` would name the blend hypothesis ("does layering A + B outperform either alone?"); levels_tested = the dev / drop / Maillard gradient across A / B / C. Chris's 2026-05-16 framing: "all the V-set experiment stuff that I do in that same framework... layer on perfectly together."

**Multi-origin blending is out of scope** — multi-coffee blend stagecraft (Tom Hutchins 2024 Ombligon + Gesha; Wataru Iidaka 2024 layered three-coffee Panama bed; Yamil Quino 2024 washed + anaerobic + mossto Bolivian trio) lives in Consciously not pursuing. Same-green is Latent's adapted form.
_Avoid_: "single-origin blending" (close — but single-origin overloads with the broader sourcing-context; same-green is more precise about the constraint), "in-lot blending" (close — but in-lot doesn't carry the *deliberate* multi-roast framing), "roast blending" (under-specified — could mean multi-origin roast-then-blend), "WBC blending experiment" (close — but the canonical noun is "same-green blending" reflecting the Latent-specific scope), "dev ladder" without "same-green" qualifier (under-specified — could mean any development gradient, including across multiple greens).

**Rest curve protocol**:
The structured rest-window experiment shape that **sequences 4 cupping events across post-roast time on one reference roast** to map the rest behavior of a specific lot. Lives in [wbc-roasting.md § Rest as a structured variable](../../docs/roasting/wbc-roasting.md). The roasting-side answer to Latent's current "freeze at peak" practice having no structured peak-detection method — WBC competitors treat rest as a strategic variable (Tom Hutchins 30 hours, Aga Rojewska 2-3 days, Lakis Psomas 10-14 days, Andrea Batacchi 20+ days, Thomas Philips flash-frozen at peak), Latent doesn't yet.

**Protocol**:
- Carve out 80g from the reference roast immediately after Day 7 evaluation: 4 × 20g portions.
- Cup each portion at a sequenced rest day: **Day 4-5** (aroma, volatility, sharpness, CO2 interference, top-note brightness) — **Day 7** (canonical pourover gate, existing reference cup) — **Day 10-12** (sweetness integration, body development) — **Day 18-21** (stability, body, florals vs fade).
- Same brewer + grinder + grind setting + recipe per cupping — rest is the only variable.
- Per-cupping records: dry / wet aroma, attack, mid-palate, finish, body, clarity, integration. Cupping notes carry the rest-day-vs-Day-7 delta ("vs Day 7: tighter finish, less aromatic lift").

**Schema-friendly**: lives on the existing `cuppings` table (no schema change). Each rest-day cupping is one `cupping` row with the same `roast_id` and `cupping_date` advancing across the curve; `rest_days` derives from `cupping_date - roast_date`. The rest curve emerges as 4 cupping rows under one roast.

**Freeze decision rule** (locked 2026-05-16 via wbc-roasting.md): **freeze when two consecutive tastings show the cup is no longer improving**. Replaces the implicit "Day 7 then freeze" cadence with an evidence-based call. Records the freeze decision + driving cup notes in `roast_learnings`.

**Today's status**: Active in Experiment status (queued for next reference roast — likely CGLE-SRUME-NATURAL-2026 or GESHA CLOUDS). Not yet executed; would be the first formal rest curve in `docs/roasting/archive.md`.

**Distinct from rest behavior** (currently in `roast_learnings`) — rest behavior is the *retrospective observation* about a lot's rest pattern (peaks early / late / plateaus / declines), often free-text. Rest curve protocol is the *structured experiment* that produces that observation. The protocol is the input; rest behavior is the output.
_Avoid_: "rest experiment" (under-specified — could mean many rest-related experiments), "rest curve" without "protocol" (overloaded — rest curve is also used informally to mean any post-roast time progression; the canonical noun for the structured experiment is "Rest curve protocol"), "4-portion cupping" (descriptive but loses the structured-experiment framing), "rest schedule" (close — but schedule is the cadence; protocol is the experiment shape).

**Long-run experiment** (future-scope architectural concept, Chris-articulated 2026-05-16):
A **multi-turn structured experiment** that operates on the same V-set-style state machine (Waiting for next batch / Waiting for next cupping / Resolved) but is **experiment-shaped rather than lot-scoped**. The architectural container for Same-green blending + Rest curve protocol + future structured experiments (water strength ladder, filter behavior test, mid-pour temperature blending, pre-ground rest, etc.) when they're formalized.

**Distinct from V-set** (lot-scoped, tests roast variables to identify the lot's reference roast) and from **Brewing iteration loop** (coffee-scoped, sequential single-recipe turns to identify the reference brew).
